Javadoc [19391,20544]
    TagElement [19399,20508]
        TextElement: Parser that can build a predicate from a string representation. The underlying syntax is quite simple, and example is [19399,19516]
        TextElement: shown below: [19521,19533]
        TextElement: <p> [19538,19541]
        TextElement: <code> [19546,19552]
        TextElement: path["/MyPath"] or (method[value="POST"] and not headersPresent[value={Content-Type, "Content-Encoding"}, ignoreTrailer=true] [19557,19682]
        TextElement: </code> [19687,19694]
        TextElement: <p> [19699,19702]
        TextElement: The following boolean operators are built in, listed in order or precedence: [19707,19783]
        TextElement: - not [19788,19793]
        TextElement: - and [19798,19803]
        TextElement: - or [19808,19812]
        TextElement: <p> [19817,19820]
        TextElement: They work pretty much as you would expect them to. All other tokens are taken [19825,19902]
        TextElement: to be predicate names. If the predicate does not require any parameters then the [19907,19987]
        TextElement: brackets can be omitted, otherwise they are mandatory. [19992,20046]
        TextElement: <p> [20051,20054]
        TextElement: If a predicate is only being passed a single parameter then the parameter name can be omitted. [20059,20153]
        TextElement: Strings can be enclosed in optional double or single quotations marks, and quotation marks can be escaped using [20158,20269]
        TextElement: <code>\"</code>. [20274,20290]
        TextElement: <p> [20295,20298]
        TextElement: Array types are represented via a comma separated list of values enclosed in curly braces. [20303,20393]
        TextElement: <p> [20398,20401]
        TextElement: TODO: should we use antlr (or whatever) here? I don't really want an extra dependency just for this... [20406,20508]
    TagElement [20517,20539]
        TextElement:  Stuart Douglas [20524,20539]
